supporters Monday that he felt \"so powerful,\" a week after being released from hospital in Washington DC, where he was treated for the illness.</p><p>The event was held outside, though few supporters were photographed wearing masks and most were packed closely together, in violation of social distancing guidelines.&#160;</p><p>\"I went through it,\" Trump said. \"Now they say I'm immune. I feel so powerful I'll walk into that audience.\"</p><p>(Trump's claim of immunity <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-claims-coronavirus-immunity-but-science-is-unclear-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">is not supported by science</a>.)</p><p>He continued: \"I'll walk in there, I'll kiss everyone in that audience. I'll kiss the guys and the beautiful women and the — I'll just give you a big fat kiss.\"</p><p>Trump's appearance at the rally came hours after his personal physician, Dr Sean Conley, announced that Trump had tested negative for the coronavirus on two consecutive days and was no longer infectious.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Eric Topol  (@EricTopol) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1315115091327475712?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 11, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>It was the first time the president's test results for the virus had been revealed since he said he tested positive on October 2.&#160;</p><p>Under <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/hcp/duration-isolation.html\">Centers of Disease Control and Prevention guidelines</a>, those who test positive are urged to isolate for 10 days, advice which the president did not follow.&#160;</p><p>In his memo, Conley did not say when the negative tests had been taken.</p><p>The test which Conley said had been used to establish whether the president is infected — the Abbott BinaxNOW test — was given emergency clearance by the Food and Drugs Administration to be used \"<a href=\"https://www.fda.gov/media/136525/download\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">within the first seven days of the onset of symptoms</a>.\"</p><p>The tests, which produce a result rapidly, are found to more frequently misdiagnose than the PCR tests, in which test results are established in a laboratory, <a href=\"https://www.technologyreview.com/2020/10/07/1009636/rapid-covid-tests-can-work-white-houses-mistakes-trump-abbott/\">according to the MIT Technology Review.&#160;</a></p><p>Conley said the tests were taken \"in context with additional clinical and laboratory data.\"</p><p>The White House earlier refused several times to disclose when Trump had last tested negative for the disease. This would have revealed how many people Trump may have exposed to the disease when infected.&#160;</p><p>Dr Anthony Fauci, a key member of the White House coronavirus task force, on Monday warned in an interview <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/10/12/health/us-coronavirus-monday/index.html\">with CNN</a> that holding mass rallies was \"asking for trouble\" as cases again surged in many second largest economy fed an improvement in domestic consumption.&#160;</p><p>Official data on Tuesday showed imports rose by 13.2% year-on-year in September, far above market expectations for an increase of 0.3%, and up from August's 2.1% drop. This was also the first increase in imports in three months, as domestic activity picked up.</p><p>Exports from China also posted solid growth, rising 9.9% year-on-year, marking the fourth consecutive month of increase in overseas sales, thanks in large part to demand for medical supplies and electronics.&#160;</p><p>\"What had been more concerning, and had been for some time, was the weakness in RICHARDS/AFP via Getty Images</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>The Mexican government says at least one of its citizens received a non-consensual surgery while detained at a US immigration facility in Irwin, Georgia.</li> \n <li>The facility made headlines last month after a whistleblower claimed numerous women were being subjected to unwanted surgeries, including hysterectomies.</li> \n <li>The Mexican government did not specify what surgery the woman had received but said it is in touch with a lawyer who is considering a class-action lawsuit.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>The Mexican government says it is consulting with a lawyer about a possible class-action lawsuit after it says one of its citizens underwent an unauthorized surgery while detained by US immigration authorities.</p>\n<p>In an <a href=\"https://www.gob.mx/sre/documentos/nota-informativa-relaciones-exteriores-no-43\">October 10 statement</a>, Mexico's foreign ministry said a woman held by Immigration and Customs Enforcement at a facility in Georgia underwent surgery to which she did not consent and was medically neglected in its aftermath.</p>\n<p>The woman was reportedly held at a facility where a whistleblower and several former detainees allege immigrants were regularly pressured into receiving unwanted and unnecessary medical operations at the hands of the facility's on-call gynecologist. At least one woman at the facility in Irwin, Georgia, said one of her Fallopian tubes <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/immigration/ice-detainee-hysterectomies-hospital/2020/09/22/aaf2ca7e-fcfd-11ea-830c-a160b331ca62_story.html\">was removed without her consent</a>.</p>\n<p>The Mexican government did not specif iy what surgery its citizen had received, but noted that it was not a hysterectomy.</p>\n<p>Given the gravity of the charge, the government said it had \"solicited the opinion of a medical specialist who, after an exhaustive review of the [medical] file, believed that there were irregularities or anomalies in the medical procedure.\"</p>\n<p>The foreign ministry said it had also received a report from another woman detained at the facility who says she underwent a gynecological procedure \"without her full consent.\"</p>\n<p>The Mexican consulate in Atlanta \"is in contact with [an] attorney who's coordinating a possible class-action lawsuit,\" Mexico's foreign ministry added.</p>\n<p>ICE did not immediately respond to a request for comment.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? CHINA OUT.\" height=\"2655\" width=\"5310\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A medical worker collects a swab from a student in Qingdao, China, on October 12, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">China Daily via REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Chinese city of Qingdao says it has tested 3 million people for COVID-19 in just 48 hours.</li>\n<li>After finding 12 new coronavirus cases on Sunday, health authorities <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-testing-qingdao-city-9-million-after-12-cases-hospital-2020-10\">pledged to test all 9 million residents</a> within a week.</li>\n<li>Qingdao's reaction shows how seriously China still takes the virus, and the scale of the drive is unheard of in the US and Europe.&#160;</li>\n<li>Authorities in many US cities and European countries have struggled to roll out comprehensive testing schemes.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A Chinese city says it has tested 3 million people for COVID-19 in just 48 hours, the latest example of just how far the US and much of Europe lag behind in terms of testing capability.&#160;</p><p>On Sunday, the eastern city of Qingdao <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-testing-qingdao-city-9-million-after-12-cases-hospital-2020-10\">announced it would test all 9 million residents</a> after identifying 12 cases of coronavirus linked to a local hospital. Officials said everyone would be tested within five days.</p><p>In a Tuesday update, the Municipal Health Commission of Qingdao said none of the 1.1 million tests that had returned so far were positive, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/virus-outbreak-asia-china-archive-qingdao-b7ec6a51bf015b4de53189f26aade8f3\">according to the Associated Press.</a></p><p>However, China's National Health Commission said Tuesday that there were six new cases of the virus in Qingdao recorded in the past 24 hours, according to the AP. The reason for the discrepancy is not clear so far.</p><p>China effectively rid itself of the coronavirus in August, having <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-reported-no-new-coronavirus-cases-as-new-hotspots-emerge-2020-5\">recorded its first day without a new locally transmitted case</a> on May 23.&#160;</p><p>The news from Qingdao after a dozen new cases shows just how seriously the country is still taking the virus.</p><p>Testing 3 million people in 48 hours is a feat that would be unheard of in cities across Europe and North America.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4647a242f43f001ddff0f7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"xi jinping china poster\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A woman with a protective face mask walks past a portrait of Chinese President Xi Jinping in Shanghai, China, on March 12, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Aly Song/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Many authorities in US cities, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/07/06/us/coronavirus-test-shortage.html\">who struggled to roll out comprehensive testing programs</a> during the worst weeks of the outbreak in July, are still <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/06/17/coronavirus-testing-fall-surge-327017\">failing to do so in the face of another surge in cases</a> this autumn and winter.</p><p>\"One of the biggest obstacles to containment has been the fact that we don't have a testing strategy and people don't know their status,\" Dr. Amesh Adalja, a senior scholar at the Johns Hopkins University Center for Health Security, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-coronavirus-testing-decline-shortages-delays-2020-8\">told Business Insider</a> in August.</p><p>\"When you look at countries that have been able to contain [the virus], they didn't do anything out of the ordinary. They tested, traced, and isolated.\"</p><p>Dr. Carolyn Cannuscio, a social epidemiologist who leads the contact-tracing program at the University of Pennsylvania, also told Business Insider: \"We have a broken testing system, and that sets us up for failure in contact tracing because people are waiting so long to get their test results that we have missed a critical period for counseling those people to stay home and avoid infecting others.\"</p><p>At one point in May the US <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-testing-per-capita-countries-ahead-of-us-2020-5\">was testing more people than any other country</a>, but it still lagged far behind Europe in terms of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-testing-per-capita-us-italy-south-korea-2020-4\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"b0fddf88d09f2399e6a081fb032234a9\">testing per capita</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f857116c255d800190b9815?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump testing US coronavirus\" height=\"2367\" width=\"4735\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump at a press briefing on coronavirus testing in the White House Rose Garden on May 11, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The UK, too, has struggled to <a href=\"https://www.standard.co.uk/news/uk/coronavirus-tests-100000-target-missed-eighth-day-a4436566.html\">meet testing targets</a>, and has made fruitless attempts to <a href=\"https://www.standard.co.uk/news/health/local-lockdowns-not-working-and-counterproductive-a4565026.html\">stamp out flare-ups in areas in the north</a> of the country.</p><p>In early September, the UK government website that allowed people to book coronavirus tests crashed, <a href=\"https://www.wired.co.uk/article/coronavirus-test-uk\">saying no tests were available.</a></p><p>China has once before tested a whole city after recording just a handful of new cases.</p><p>All 11 million residents of Wuhan — where <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-outbreak-wuhan-timeline-earlier-than-officials-say-2020-4\">the outbreak began in December 2019</a> and which was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-wuhan-after-lockdown-photos-2020-4\">locked down for 76 days</a> in early 2020 — were tested over a 10-day period in May.</p><p>As of Monday evening, China has recorded 85,591 cases of COVID-19 and 4,634 deaths, <a href=\"http://www.nhc.gov.cn/xcs/yqtb/202010/400a3f95e1be4aa7b702ac45b96570f2.shtml\">according to the country's National Health Commission.</a></p><p>In comparison, as of Tuesday morning, the US has recorded more than 7.8 million confirmed cases of COVID-19 and 215,086 deaths, <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/map.html\">according to a tracker from Johns Hopkins University.</a></p><p>President Donald Trump announced he had tested positive for COVID-19 on October 2. Since then he has returned to the campaign trail and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-claims-coronavirus-immunity-but-science-is-unclear-2020-10\">claimed that he is \"immune\" to the coronavirus</a>, even though there are no indicators that could reliably determine this.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Germany.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>German staff at Amazon are striking during the e-commerce giant's annual <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-prime-day-best-deals\">Prime Day event</a> on Tuesday and Wednesday over pay and conditions in its warehouses since the outbreak of the pandemic.</p><p>Workers at seven Amazon warehouses in cities including Leipzig and Koblenz&#160;are&#160;<a href=\"https://www.br.de/nachrichten/bayern/mitarbeiter-ausgeblutet-wieder-streik-bei-amazon-in-graben,SDGu51g\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.br.de/nachrichten/bayern/mitarbeiter-ausgeblutet-wieder-streik-bei-amazon-in-graben,SDGu51g\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">striking in shifts</a> to avoid large crowds.</p><p>The country's second-largest union, Verdi, said it was organizing the strike because staff have been working \"without adequate protection,\" and haven't been compensated for the additional stress of working during the pandemic.</p><p>An Amazon spokesperson told Business Insider that the strikes will not impact its deliveries in Germany, the company's second-biggest market after the US.</p><p>The company already offers \"excellent pay, benefits, and opportunities for career growth,\" they added, with a safe working environment that is \"set up to help them succeed.\"</p><p>The company told <a href=\"https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-amazon-com-primeday-germany/amazon-workers-in-germany-strike-on-prime-day-idUKKBN26Y0XF?il=0\">Reuters</a>&#160;that most employees in Germany were working as normal.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.verdi.de/presse/pressemitteilungen/++co++06a24c9c-0a40-11eb-8d6c-001a4a16012a\">Orhan Akman, Verdi's retail representative</a>, pointed out that at the end of May, the company scrapped a coronavirus bonus of 2 euros ($2.36) an hour, just two months after it was introduced.&#160;</p><p>Amazon can \"certainly\" afford to pay staff the bonus, Akman claimed, because it doesn't face the same problems that are causing bricks and mortar retailers to fold during the pandemic.</p><p>Amazon should make the bonus a permanent salary increase for all staff, Akman added, \"because employees generate the company's profits.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-has-a-sexist-and-toxic-culture-some-employees-say-2020-9\">Leaked emails show a high-profile engineer left Amazon after filing sexual harassment claims to HR in 2018. Now she's speaking out about what she calls a 'toxic' work culture for women.</a></em></p><p>Verdi also organized a strike for Amazon workers in June over safety concerns after staff at a logistics center tested positive for COVID-19.</p><p>Christy Hoffman, the general secretary of UNI Global Union, an international union group of which Verdi is a member, said: \"Amazon has failed to ensure workers' safety, and we fear that influx of orders and the gruelling Prime Day pace will make a bad situation even worse.\"</p><p>Germany is Amazon's biggest market after the US, with its turnover <a href=\"https://www.amcham.de/newsboard/news/top-50-ranking-amazon-ford-and-exxonmobil-at-the-forefront-of-the-top-selling-us-companies-in-germany\">reaching 19.85 billion euros ($23.40 billion) in 2019</a>, according to the American Chamber of Commerce in Germany.</p><p>This meant that for the first time it had the highest turnover of any US company in Germany, pushing automaker Ford off the top spot.&#160;</p><p>Amazon now has 13 logistics sites in Germany, with two more opening by the end of 2020, and a workforce of around 20,000.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 20:57:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 20:57:00","title":"Facebook donated $1.3 million to the UK's World War II code-breaking hub, Bletchley Park","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-donates-1-million-to-bletchley-park-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f857d48c255d800190b9829?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bletchley Park\" height=\"1687\" width=\"2250\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bletchley Park, the UK&#39;s codebreaking HQ in World War II.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jack Taylor/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Facebook is donating &#163;1 million ($1.3 million) to Bletchley Park, the UK's World War II code-breaking HQ.</li>\n<li>Bletchley Park is now a historical site, and has seen a dip in visitor numbers due to the pandemic.</li>\n<li>\"Facebook simply would not exist today if not for Bletchley Park,\" Facebook CTO Mike Schroepfer said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook on Tuesday made a public donation of £1 million ($1.3 million) to Bletchley Park, the UK historical site which Facebook describes as the \"birthplace of the computer.\"</p><p>Bletchley Park, a stately home in southern England, was the UK's codebreaking hub during World War II. It was where the first Enigma-encrypted Nazi messages were broken in 1940, and where famous British computer scientist Alan Turing did much of his work.</p><p>The site is now a historical tourist spot, and has seen a significant drop in visitor numbers since the pandemic began.</p><p>Facebook Chief Technology Officer Mike Schroepfer wrote in a <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/bletchley-park-donation/\">blog post</a> that Facebook's donation was prompted by Bletchley Park's formative role in early, foundational computer science.</p><p>\"Facebook simply would not exist today if not for Bletchley Park,\" Schroepfer wrote.</p><p>\"By figuring out how to crack the Nazis' secret communications, the almost 10,000 people who worked at Bletchley Park during World War II — 75% of them women — changed the course of the war and saved millions of lives.</p><p>\"They did it by building the world's first programmable digital computer and laying the foundations of modern computer science. Ideas developed at Bletchley Park remain at the heart of cutting-edge research in fields like artificial intelligence, online security and cryptography today, more than 80 years after the first codebreakers set up shop there.\"</p><p>The CEO of Bletchley Park, Iain Standen, said in a statement that he was \"very grateful to Facebook for their generous donation,\" and that the money would help it \"keep its doors open for future generations.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a trends is the wave of special-purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, that have launched IPOs at such a torrid pace that they're on track to raise more than triple last year's totals.</p><p>So far this year, 138 SPACs, aka \"blank-check firms,\" have raised $53.8 billion, according to the website SPAC Research. There are now 205 shell companies with $67 billion to spend on bringing other companies public, the data provider said.</p><p>There's an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-spac-underwriters-law-firms-investors-blank-check-volume-fees-2020-9?r=spac-teaser\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">entire ecosystem of advisers, salespeople, and lawyers</a> increasingly pitching blank-check companies to investment platforms and wealthy people. Asset managers like Fidelity, T. Rowe Price, and Capital Research are also increasingly participating in the market, lending an additional aura of respectability to what had once been considered a back corner of the financial markets.</p><p>As the market has gained more respectability, the names of the players driving its growth have changed. Investors typically expect the month before the US election to bring volatility to the stock market. But some analysts are predicting that volatility could continue days and weeks after election day, if the result wasn't immediately clear.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original Free usage gets you alerts, livestreaming, and two-way audio. The basic Ring Protect plan and the Protect Plus plans are essentially extra storage options for video recordings so that you can review a captured event later if you miss the alert.</p><p>The basic Ring Protect plan costs $3 a month and lets you record and share captured video from motion detection and doorbell rings for up to 60 days, and it'll store photos for seven days, from a single device.</p><p>The Ring Protect Plus plan costs $10 per month and comes with unlimited video storage for an unlimited number of Ring devices. If you have the Ring Alarm, you may already have this plan, as it also encompasses monitoring and cellular backup for that device.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5f81109602495a32d1799943\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5f81109602495a32d1799943&type=medium&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><p>The standard (and newest) <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07WGJ8XWZ?tag=biip_101320_amazon-prime-day-2020-20&linkCode=ogi&th=1&psc=1=1&#38;psc=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Ring Video Doorbell</a> was released in 2020. It can record and stream 1080p footage and comes with improved motion detection, privacy zone settings, and better night vision compared to the original first-generation Ring Video Doorbell. Being a smart doorbell, you can stream, control, and speak with visitors via the Ring app on mobile devices. You can use existing doorbell wiring if your home has it, or the Ring Video Doorbell can be powered by an on-board rechargeable battery.&#160;</p><p>As far as deals go, it's a great entry-level option that lets you test the waters of adding smart devices to your home. Even though the Ring Video Doorbell has entry-level pricing, especially with this $70 Amazon Prime Day deal, it's advanced and featured enough to be sufficient for the vast majority of people wanting to get a better idea of who or what is lingering outside their front door.&#160;</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5e9a0045d5873a7c726403c5\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5e9a0045d5873a7c726403c5&type=medium&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><p>The <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0849J7W5X?tag=biip_101320_amazon-prime-day-2020-20&linkCode=ogi&th=1&psc=1=1&#38;psc=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Ring Video Doorbell 3</a> offers somewhat more advanced features than the standard Video Doorbell above. Video resolution is the same at 1080p, but the video's field-of-view is slightly wider with an extra five degrees. It can connect to a 5GHz WiFi network, which is better suited for video streaming and could make for a better video stream when you watch on your mobile device. Like the standard doorbell, it can be powered by existing wiring or a rechargeable battery pack.&#160;</p><p>The 30% deal is good to have if you're after those upgrades. It's also sleeker than the traditional Ring Doorbell design.</p><p>All this said, there are some caveats. It's designed to replace your existing peephole, and Ring says the process takes five minutes and doesn't require any drilling or wiring. It can be easily removed and taken to another apartment, too — just make sure you keep the original peephole. Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Rajeev Misra, the CEO of SoftBank's Vision Fund, plans to launch Vision Fund 2's own special-acquisition company. He said he would outline details in the next two weeks.</strong></li><li><strong>The blank-check company will be operated by the fund's investment advisers and is expected to seek external funds along with SoftBank's own capital, CNBC reported.</strong></li><li><strong>The SPAC would provide SoftBank with a new investment route, combining the group's expertise in tech investments and its new focus on public stock trading.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Rajeev Misra, the head of SoftBank's $100 billion Vision Fund, is joining the SPAC race, as he seeks to capitalize on the trendy new investment vehicle.</p><p>At the 2020 <a href=\"https://milkeninstitute.org/events/global-conference-2020\">Milken Institute Global Conference</a> on Monday, Misra said he would outline plans for the blank-check company in the next two weeks, but did not provide further details.&#160;</p><p>The SPAC will be handled by Vision Fund 2's investment advisers, and will include capital from both external investors and the fund itself, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/12/softbank-vision-fund-head-rajeev-misra-vision-fund-2-is-backing-spac.html\">CNBC said</a>, citing a source.</p><p>The Vision Fund is primarily known for its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/running-list-softbank-investments-2017-7\">investments in startups</a>. The group has poured cash into technology-forward companies including Uber, WeWork, Slack, Nvidia, and ARM.&#160;</p><p><strong><em>Read More:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\"><em>The global investment strategist at a $44 billion ETF shop explains why the pandemic-fueled boom of online retail is set to accelerate — and shares 5 stocks to watch other than Amazon ahead of its Prime Day</em></a></p><p>The follow-up fund, Vision Fund 2, is aimed at investments in <a href=\"https://www.sme10x.com/10x-industry/softbanks-vision-fund-2-announced-here-are-all-the-details#:~:text=The%20Vision%20Fund%202%20is,in%20Artificial%20Intelligence%20based%20technology.&text=SoftBank's%20initial%20Vision%20Fund%20of,Ola%2C%20WeWork%2C%20and%20more.ore.\">artificial intelligence-based technology</a>. The blank-check venture would combine the Japanese conglomerate's expertise in tech investments and its new focus on public stock trading.</p><p>Earlier this year, SoftBank's asset management business <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/softbank-invests-billions-tech-giants-stock-market-tesla-amazon-netflix-2020-8-1029513600#\">invested nearly $3.9 billion</a> across some of the world's most popular stocks including Amazon, Tesla, Alphabet, and Netflix. It planned to invest more than $10 billion in public companies.</p><p>Wall Street's obsession with SPACs has led to a surge in popularity this year, with many high-profile investors piling into this alternative investment route.&#160;</p><p>Over $53 billion has been raised across 138 SPAC IPOs so far this year, according to <a href=\"https://spacinsider.com/stats/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SPACInsider.com</a>. Last year saw only $13.6 billion raised across 59 deals. The average size of SPAC IPOs climbed to $388 million this year, from $230 million in 2019.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em href=\"https://www.amazon.co.uk/amazon-smart-plug-works-with-alexa/dp/B082YTKC47/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2ZU63H2PDDQ9V&dchild=1&keywords=amazon%2Bsmart%2Bplug&qid=1602588186&s=amazon-devices&sprefix=amazon%2Bsmart%2Camazon-devices%2C143&sr=1-1&th=1es%2C143&#38;sr=1-1&#38;th=1\">Amazon href=\"https://www.ons.gov.uk/employmentandlabourmarket/peopleinwork/employmentandemployeetypes/bulletins/employmentintheuk/october2020\">data released</a> by the Office of National Statistics on Tuesday.&#160;</p><p>The number of people claiming jobless benefits rose to 2.7 million in September — an increase of 1.5 million since March 2020, the ONS said.</p><p>People who were laid off, or voluntarily left jobs, rose o 227,000 in the three-month period to August, up by 113,000 from the same period the previous year, the largest annual increase since April to June 2009, during the financial crisis.</p><p>Redundancies in the quarter reached the highest level since May to July 2009, ONS said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8559bbc255d800190b97f6?format=jpeg\" as infections surge across the country. the unemployment rate is not high by historical standards, the picture is clearly deteriorating, according to Laith Khalaf, a financial analyst at AJ Bell.</p><p>\"We're beginning to see what the Revenue fell 7% from the year-ago period as thriving trading desks fell short of offsetting a consumer banking slump. Increased loan-loss reserves led net income to tank 34% from the year-ago period.</p><p>Citigroup shares gained as much as 2% in early Tuesday trading.</p><p><strong>Here are the key numbers:&#160;</strong></p><ul><li><strong>Revenue:</strong>&#160;$17.3 billion, versus the $17.2 billion estimate from analysts surveyed by Bloomberg</li><li><strong>Adjusted earnings per share:</strong>&#160;$1.40 per share, versus the 92 cent estimate</li><li><strong>Net income:</strong>&#160;$3.2 billion, versus the $1.8 billion estimate</li></ul><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"4\" data-analytics-module=\"\">The global investment strategist at a $44 billion ETF shop explains why the pandemic-fueled boom of online retail is set to accelerate — and shares 5 stocks to watch other than Amazon ahead of its Prime Day</a></em></p><p>Global Consumer Banking revenues fell 13% to $7.2 billion as client spending remained stifled.&#160;</p><p>\"We continue to navigate the effects of the COVID-19 pandemic extremely well. Credit costs have stabilized, deposits continued to increase, and revenues are up 3% year-to-date,\" CEO Michael Corbat said in a statement. \"Although Global Consumer Banking revenues remained lower as a result of the pandemic, we did see higher activity in our mortgage and wealth management products.\"</p><p>Net credit losses climbed roughly 200% from the year-ago period to $329 million. The bank's reserves for soured loans grew 111% from the year-ago period to $26.4 billion, or 4% of loans.</p><p>The bank's third-quarter figures reveal continued strength as the financial sector rebounds from the pandemic's economic fallout. The quarter saw the US relax more lockdown measures before a second wave of infections prompted some fears of resumed quarantines. Several gauges of economic growth moderated their pace of improvement, leaving some looking to Congress to reinvigorate the recovery with another stimulus measure.</p><p>Citi's second-quarter results <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/citigroup-stock-earnings-second-quarter-report-coronavirus-beat-recession-economy-2020-7-1029392117\">bore the brunt of the coronavirus' hit</a>, with net income contracting 73% from the year-ago period. Still, earnings and revenue beat expectations as the company's outperforming trading desks offset losses in its consumer banking arm.</p><p>The Tuesday report kicks off an earnings season set to reveal how companies performed through the slowing bounce-back. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/jpm-stock\">JPMorgan</a> — the first major bank to report — <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/jpmorgan-q3-earnings-beat-estimates-trading-revenue-jumps-2020-10-1029673525\">beat expectations for revenue and profit</a> over the period as target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-outlook-market-impact-contested-us-elections-deutsche-bank-2020-10\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Deutsche Bank scoured 200 years of US history to uncover how investors should handle a contested election — including 3 past examples and how markets responded</a></em>&#160;</p><p>He thinks it is still too early to invest in some airline and cruise stocks, which have been among the worst-hit by widespread coronavirus lockdowns.&#160;</p><p>\"You probably want to stay away from the other tail, which are airlines, cruise lines [and] energy — the really distressed deep value stuff,\" Mills said. \"Find yourself somewhere in the middle. We like industrials. We like materials.\"</p><p>Shares in cruise operator <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ccl-stock\">Carnival </a>and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nclh-stock\">Norwegian Cruise Line Holdings&#160;</a>are both down around 70% since the start of the year.&#160;</p><p>Mills said the broader market environment has once again highlighted whether investors are rotating away from growth and into value.</p><p>\"Right now, all of that stems from stimulus talks,\" he said. \"You are seeing that rotation from growth into value fade a little bit.\"</p><p>The number of long-term unemployed people is still rising, despite gains in the number of workers on non-farm payrolls in the last few months, Mills said.</p><p>\"We are seeing cracks in consumer incomes,\" he said. \"The question is do those cracks get filled with additional stimulus? If they do I think the rotation can happen quicker but if they don't then they have to heal on their own and I think you have this default trade back to growth like we are seeing,\" he added.&#160;</p><p>Democrats and Republicans have been at loggerheads over the size and reach of another package of measures to support the real economy since July.&#160;</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">The global investment strategist at a $44 billion ETF shop explains why the pandemic-fueled boom of online retail is set to accelerate — and shares 5 stocks to watch other than Amazon ahead of its Prime Day</a></em></p><p>The latest exchange of views between the two sides took place over the weekend, when President Donald Trump's team <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-congress-relief/white-house-seeks-limited-coronavirus-relief-bill-promises-further-talks-on-broader-stimulus-idUSKBN26W0QO\">proposed</a> a $1.8 trillion stimulus package over the weekend.</p><p>The measures would include a $400 boost in weekly unemployment insurance, $1,200 stimulus checks for US adults, and $1,000 checks for every child. class=\"copyright\">Amazon</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Amazon has launched an augmented reality (AR) app that brings printed objects on its delivery boxes to life.</li>\n<li>Users scan a QR code on a box to bring up a customizable AR version of the object, which will stay on your phone's camera as you move around.</li>\n<li>Videos and images show pumpkins, augmented reality app from the e-commerce giant.</p><p>A promotional video for the <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1519505870\">\"Amazon Augmented Reality\" app</a> shows users drawing a face on a pumpkin printed on Amazon Halloween delivery boxes. They then scan the QR code to bring the pumpkin to life as a jack o'lantern, which follows the phone's camera around the room.</p><p>You can change the color of the pumpkin and add accessories in the app, too.</p><p>So far the jack o'lantern is the only function available on the free app, but <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id1519505870#?platform=ipad\">photos on the App Store page</a> suggest the retailer will distribute other shipping boxes with different AR functions.</p><p>One photo shows a delivery box being transformed into a blue car, for example. Another shows a dog's head replaced by a pumpkin wearing a top hat and a monocle.&#160;</p><p>The app is available on both iOS and Android, and the description says it is \"fun way to reuse your Amazon boxes until you're ready to drop them in the recycling bin.\"</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/UTnjUxQNZsc\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p>The video also shows the on-screen pumpkin following a user's face as they turn their head. Amazon notes in the App Store description that if you have Apple's TrueDepth camera technology, which renders 3D photos, the app will track your facial movements.</p><p>The app comes with sound effects, too.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/congress-antitrust-google-amazon-web-services-cloud-acquisitions-2020-10\">House lawmakers accuse Google Cloud and Amazon Web Services for buying companies to \"solidify and expand their dominance\"</a></em></p><p>Amazon notes on its website that its team is <a href=\"https://amazonar.app/halloween\">creating more augmented reality experiences.</a></p><p>The app can only be used on Amazon boxes and isn't compatible with other QR codes. But if users don't have a physical box, they can test the function out with <a href=\"https://amazonar.app/halloween\">a virtual box on Amazon's website</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Crest 3D White Strips Professional Express 7-count down to $30 (originally $40)</a> [You save $10]</li></ul><h2>What is Target Deal Days?</h2><p>Target's sale, aptly named <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-online-sales-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Deal Days</a>, offers major savings on hundreds of thousands of products. Target-exclusive brands also see discounts. This year's sale focuses on holiday deals and prices. The deals are available online, so shoppers won't have to brave the typical holiday shopping crowds of past years.</p><h2>When is Target Deal Days?</h2><p>This year, the event began on October 13 and runs through October 14, the same dates as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-prime-day-best-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amazon Prime Day 2020</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-buy-prime-day-deals-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Best Buy's deal event</a>. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-prime-day-sale-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Walmart's Big Save Event</a> is also running right now, though it lasts for a longer time period from October 11 through October 15. Target has also announced season-long savings after Deal Days, starring weeklong discounts and daily digital deals beginning November 1.&#160;</p><h2>Can anyone shop Deal Days?</h2><p>Yes, the sale is available for anyone to shop online, no membership required. Discounts are available to all shoppers, though <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/target-redcard-compared-to-amazon-prime-at-whole-foods-2018-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Target RedCard</a> holders get an extra 5% off purchases. The sale does not extend to in-store purchases.</p><h2>How do I prepare for Deal Days?</h2><p>Now that the event is live, the best way to get the best prices is to download the <a href=\"https://goto.target.com/c/196318/81938/2092?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.target.com%2Fc%2Ftarget-app%2F-%2FN-4th2r\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Target App</a> and enroll in the company's free loyalty program, <a href=\"https://www.target.com/circle/dashboard\">Target Circle</a> to reap extra discounts. Other than that, all that's left to do is shop the huge sale and keep an eye on this page, where we'll highlight the best deals from Deal Days as we find them.&#160;</p><h2>What deals are available during Deal Days?</h2><p>This year's deals cover products across all categories including tech, fashion, beauty, household essentials, and more. Just like last year, we're seeing discounts on popular brands like KitchenAid and Samsung, plus Target's in-house labels. A handful of products, like the JBL Flip 5 and Revlon Salon One-Step Dryer and Volumizer, are even lower prices than that of Amazon this Prime Day.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original At the height of the pandemic in April, the state peaked at 799 deaths in a single day.</li>\n<li>Gov. Andrew Cuomo has blamed the rise in hospitalizations on virus hotspots that the state is monitoring, which are largely Orthodox Jewish communities.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>New York state is experiencing a dramatic rise in coronavirus hospitalizations, which are up 97% from September 1.</p><p>On Sunday, 878 people in the state were reported as being currently hospitalized, compared to 445 on September 1, <a href=\"https://forward.ny.gov/daily-hospitalization-summary-region\">according to state data</a>. The 97% increase&#160;<a href=\"https://www.syracuse.com/coronavirus/2020/10/coronavirus-in-ny-hospitalizations-rise-to-878-up-over-97-since-sept-1.html\">first reported by Syracuse.com</a>.</p><p>The number of patients in intensive care is also up by 58% since September 1. The state recorded <a href=\"https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/governor-cuomo-updates-new-yorkers-states-progress-during-covid-19-pandemic-46\">185</a> people in intensive care units on Sunday, compared to <a href=\"https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/audio-rush-transcript-governor-cuomo-updates-new-yorkers-states-progress-during-covid-19-4\">117</a> on September 1.</p><p>The seven-day rolling average of hospital beds available across the reason remain at 25%, and average share of ICU beds across the region at 36%, <a href=\"https://forward.ny.gov/early-warning-monitoring-dashboard\">state data said</a>.</p><p>The number of coronavirus deaths in New York remain low, however, with the state <a href=\"https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/governor-cuomo-updates-new-yorkers-states-progress-during-covid-19-pandemic-46\">saying</a> it had recorded 12 new deaths on Sunday. For comparison, statewide deaths reached a <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/10/nyregion/new-york-coronavirus-death-count.html\">high of 799</a> at the virus' peak in the region in April.</p><p>The rise in hospitalizations is no doubt a concern for New Yorkers who weathered what was, at one point, the largest outbreak in the US.</p><p>But Gov. Andrew Cuomo sought to ease some of those concerns in a <a href=\"https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/governor-cuomo-updates-new-yorkers-states-progress-during-covid-19-pandemic-46\">Monday conference call with reporters</a>, blaming the hospitalizations on a select number of hotspots in the state.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f85791f91aa9e001880b32f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"andrew cuomo\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>New York Gov. Andrew Cuomo at a September 8, 2020 news conference.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/new-york-state-gov-andrew-cuomo-speaks-at-a-news-conference-news-photo/1271366253?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Spencer Platt/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The governor blamed the increase in hospitalizations on coronavirus clusters throughout the state that public-health officials are monitoring.</p><p>These \"red zone\" areas — which include parts of Brooklyn and Queens, as well as Broome, Orange, and Rockland counties — have since Friday been under new lockdown regulations, which closed schools and nonessential businesses, and banned large gatherings and religious ceremonies over 10 people.&#160;</p><p>The move to limit religious gatherings has largely angered New York's Orthodox Jewish communities, which believe the state is infringing upon their rights to worship.</p><p>Last week, members of one such community <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nyc-orthodox-jews-protest-local-lockdown-face-masks-bonfire-2020-10\">started a bonfire in the middle of a Brooklyn street</a>, where they burned face masks in protest of the new measures.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7d95b0282c500018c79088?format=jpeg\" alt=\"gathered around fire\" height=\"1125\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An Orthodox Jewish community burning face masks in a bonfire on October 6, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.nbcnewyork.com/news/local/ultra-orthodox-community-members-gather-to-protest-new-covid-restrictions/2655635/\" target=\"_blank\">NBC New York</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In a Sunday call with reporters, Cuomo said that the infections are predominantly coming from Jewish communities which have continued to hold large religious services, according to the <a href=\"https://www.timesunion.com/news/article/New-York-COVID-19-hospitalizations-up-73-percent-15637694.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Times Union</a>.&#160;</p><p>\"I understand the desire to hold large religious ceremonies,\" Cuomo said.&#160;\"I understand how important it is to their culture and religion. 20:57:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 20:57:00","title":"Boris Johnson overruled scientists who told him to introduce a lockdown three weeks ago, while ignoring warnings that his plans won't stop the coronavirus","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-ignored-advice-lock-down-uk-three-weeks-ago-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img Britain October 13, 2020. REUTERS/Simon Dawson\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Britain&#39;s Prime Minister Boris Johnson and Chancellor of the Exchequer Rishi Sunak arrive for a Cabinet meeting, in London, Britain October 13, 2020. REUTERS/Simon Dawson\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Simon Dawson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Boris Johnson ignored advice from the team of scientists who advise the government on its coronavirus response, according to newly published papers.</li>\n<li>The group of scientists, who comprise the SAGE committee, told Boris Johnson to introduce a 14-day 'circuit-breaker' lockdown as long as three weeks ago.</li>\n<li>They also told the PM to introduce further national measures, including a ban on household mixing and the closure of pubs and restaurants.</li>\n<li>Johnson ignored the advice, and yesterday introduced an alternative three-tier local system where different areas face different restrictions.</li>\n<li>The Prime Minister's chief medical adviser said on Monday that the government's new measures will not be enough to stop the second wave of the coronavirus currently gripping the UK.</li>\n<li>Other papers published this week reveal that the UK's much-hyped track-and-trace system is failing to contain coronavirus transmissions.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Boris Johnson ignored advice to introduce a second national lockdown three weeks ago, according to <a href=\"https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/925853/S0768_Fifty-eighth_SAGE_meeting_on_Covid-19.pdf\">newly published documents</a> which illustrate an extraordinary spat between ministers and the scientists who advise them.</p><p>The scientific advisory group for emergencies (SAGE) advised the prime minister to introduce a raft of measures to try and contain the rate of Covid-19 transmissions in a Zoom meeting three weeks ago.</p><p>Boris Johnson reportedly sided with \"hawks\" in his Cabinet, including Chancellor Rishi Sunak, and refused to consider the measures because he feared the damage they would do to the economy.</p><p>The measures suggested included a two-week \"circuit breaker\" lockdown similar to the one imposed in March, a national ban on household mixing, and the closure of all restaurants, pubs, cafes, gyms, and hairdressers.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/925856/S0770_NPIs_table__pivot_.pdf\">papers also reveal</a> that Johnson was warned that plans he did later enact to introduce a curfew on pubs and restaurants would only have a \"marginal impact\" on the spread of the virus.</p><p>The prime minister <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-lockdown-boris-johnson-3-tiered-system-england-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">instead on Monday announced</a> a \"three-tier\" system of local lockdowns, where areas which faced the highest incidence rate of Covid-19 would face the harshest measures.</p><p>He told parliament on Monday: \"The number of cases has quadrupled in the last three weeks, there are now more people in hospital with Covid than when we went into lockdown on March 23 and deaths are already rising.\"</p><p>Currently the city of Liverpool is in the highest category, \"very high risk,\" due to a soaring infection rate and rapidly filling intensive care units which threaten to overwhelm local NHS trusts.</p><p>The extraordinary rift between Johnson and his team of scientific advisers was illustrated at Monday's Downing Street press conference, where Johnson and Chris Whitty, the chief medical officer, were explaining the new three-tier lockdown system.</p><p>Whitty pointedly said that even the harshest local measures in the new system would not be \"sufficient\" to limit the spread of Covid-19.</p><p>He said that he was \"very confident that the measures that are currently in place are helping to slow the virus, and these measures will help to slow it further\" but added: \"I am not confident - and nor is anybody confident - that the Tier 3 proposals for the highest rates if we did the absolute base case and nothing more, would be enough to get on top of it.\"</p><p>A senior minister on Tuesday admitted that lockdown measures would \"probably\" have to get tougher to contain the virus. Robert Jenrick, the housing minister, <a href=\"https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-8834273/Lockdown-probably-tougher-admit-ministers-amid-SAGE-row.html\">dismissed claims</a> the measures were not \"robust\" enough but said councils should show \"leadership\" by introducing stricter measures.</p><p>\"We probably will need to go further,\" he said. \"But we want to design these steps jointly between ourselves and local government.\"</p><p>In <a href=\"https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/925854/S0769_Summary_of_effectiveness_and_harms_of_NPIs.pdf\">another document</a> which could prove highly damaging to the government, the SAGE group of scientists said that the £12 billion \"test-and-trace\" programme, which Johnson has described as \"world-beating\" is having only a \"marginal\" impact on reducing the spread of the virus because it is not tracing enough people, and many of those contacted are simply ignoring advice to self-isolate.</p><p>SAGE suggested that the programme's effectiveness would likely \"further decline\" as the virus continued to spread.</p><p>\"The relatively low levels of engagement with the system... coupled with testing delays and likely poor rates of adherence with self-isolation suggests that this system is having a marginal impact on transmission at the moment,\" the scientists wrote.</p><p>\"'Unless the system grows at the same rate as the epidemic, and support is given to people to enable them to adhere to self-isolation, it is likely that the impact of Test, Trace and Isolate will further decline in the future.\"</p><div savings of $26.</li><li>Normally, a single <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07HHW9H9X?tag=biip_101320_amazon-prime-day-2020-20&linkCode=ogi&th=1&psc=1=1&#38;psc=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">West Loop</a> goes for anywhere from $14-$21, depending on the color, so this deal essentially makes them buy-one-get-one-free (great for gift-giving during the holidays).</li><li>This spill-proof button-operated travel mug is currently our best overall pick in our <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-travel-mug\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow Loop</a> keeps coffee hot for hours, as any good travel mug should. But there's one aspect in which it truly excels, and that's in ensuring your coffee stays exactly where it should — in the mug. It's leak-proof, but it's also spill-proof. Yes, those are two different things.</p><p>Where a normal travel mug lid can be left open, leading to spills from an errant elbow, the Autoseal lives up to its name by sealing itself whenever it's not being drunk from. When you're ready for a drink, you depress the button on the lid. As soon as you let go, your mug promptly seals itself.</p><p>This <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-prime-day-best-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Prime Day</a>, two-packs of the useful mug are on sale for $18.99 (previously $44.99), essentially making the mugs buy-one-get-one-free. A single mug normally costs anywhere from $14 to $21 depending on the color you choose. While the two-pack colors are limited, it might be worth it to compromise for the savings.</p><p>There is one caveat to this mug. The lid of the West Loop is structured a bit differently, so it may not have the same issue, but be sure to thoroughly wash your travel mug after each use and let it air dry completely.</p><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7dd8bd94fce90018f7b9e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mark zuckerberg facebook\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Facebook co-founder and CEO Mark Zuckerberg.\n<p class=\"copyright\">The Asahi Shimbun via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Facebook on Monday announced it would ban any content that denies the existence of the Holocaust.</li>\n<li>The social media company told Bloomberg this policy would not extend to other historical genocides including the Rwandan and Armenian genocides.</li>\n<li>It did not clarify why denial of these genocides was still allowed on Facebook.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook's new <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-bans-holocaust-denial-posts-after-refusing-removal-content-moderation-2020-10\">ban on Holocaust denial</a> won't extend to other genocides, the company told <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-10-12/facebook-to-ban-posts-that-deny-holocaust-in-reversal-of-policy\">Bloomberg</a> on Monday.</p><p>Facebook said its ban wouldn't extend to, for example, the Rwandan or Armenian genocides.</p><p>Roughly 800,000 ethnic Tutsi people were killed in the <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-26875506\">Rwandan genocide</a> in 1994. In Turkey between 1914 and 1923, 1.5 million Armenians were killed by the Ottoman Empire.</p><p>Denial of the Armenian genocide is particularly rife, as the Turkish government refuses to recognize it. The US government <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/ewelinaochab/2019/12/17/denial-is-the-final-stage-of-genocide-the-armenians-know-it-best/#5b767c9770b1\">voted last year to officially recognize the genocide</a>, but it is in a minority of countries that do so.</p><p>Facebook did not explain its rationale to Bloomberg for why it was not extending its ban to these and other genocides, and it was not immediately available to comment when contacted by Business Insider.</p><p>In its Monday <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/removing-holocaust-denial-content/\">blog post</a> explaining why it was reversing its previous policy to allow Holocaust denial on the platform, Facebook said its decision was&#160;\"supported by the well-documented rise in anti-Semitism globally and the alarming level of ignorance about the Holocaust, especially among young people.\"</p><p>It added that Holocaust education is \"a key component in combatting anti-Semitism.\"</p><p>Facebook's CEO Mark Zuckerberg had previously said that he thought Holocaust denial was abhorrent, but didn't think it should be censored from the platform.</p><p>\"I'm Jewish, and there's a set of people who deny that the Holocaust happened. I find that deeply offensive. But at the end of the day, I don't believe that our platform should take that down because I think there are things that different people get wrong,\" he told <a event that his performance against Biden was \"crappy,\" in footage published by Huff Post.</li>\n<li>Moore spoke at an event in Washington organised by pro-Trump group FreedomWorks.</li>\n<li>Trump has previously praised Moore as \"a great pro-growth economist and a truly fine person\"</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>An economic advisor to Donald Trump was filmed describing his performance in the recent debate against Joe Biden as \"crappy\" in newly-released footage from earlier this month.</p><p>Stephen Moore, who Trump has <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2019/05/how-did-stephen-moore-get-picked-federal-reserve/588502/\">previously described</a> as \"a great pro-growth economist and a truly fine person\", made the remarks earlier this month at the Election Protection Summit in Washington organised by pro-Trump group FreedomWorks.</p><p>\"It was not a great performance by Trump; in fact, I thought it was a pretty crappy performance,\" he told the crowd, <a href=\"https://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/entry/trump-stephen-moore-crappy-debate_n_5f84e71bc5b6e6d033a68092?ri18n=true&guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly9jb25zZW50LnlhaG9vLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAADrAbCYCCsjE0nvJLddTLcXdmyQTMkCigWfU8jQXKyaul3IgzZsJQTobd-Q3LmU9gAUB2Cqv42Gy7uXFwizkx2QJ6C6oKuX2sa51OuzMzTZYYRWeRKeBBMaTS0YZ4ljDH58UdBnzu1ZCyv3h1WQ-9q8ZkmRVdn_CHfJPXYocGi0-HfJPXYocGi0-\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in footage published by Huff Post</a> and acquired by Wisconsin-based watchdog Documented.</p><p>Moore also said that Trump had put in an \"awful\" performance in his first debate with Democratic candidate Hilary Clinton in the run-up to the 2016 election.</p><p>\"Oh my God, he was so bad in that debate, just awful,\" Moore reportedly said at the event on October 2.</p><p>However, he added that Trump had \"rallied\" and \"clobbered\" Clinton in the next debate and that \"God willing\" that is \"what's going to happen\" at the next debate between Trump and Biden before next month's presidential election.</p><p>Moore added that he thought the election would be a \"really tight.\"</p><p>The first televised debate between Trump and Biden took place at the end of last month and received mostly negative reviews.</p><p>The 90-minute debate was characterised by repeated interruptions from Trump and bad-natured exchanges between the two candidates. Speaking shortly after the debate,&#160;Biden said Trump's performance, in which he spoke over Biden several times and made a number of false statements, was a \"national embarrassment.\" At one point during the debate, Biden told to Trump to \"shut up\" and later called him a \"clown.\"&#160;</p><p>In the same debate, Trump refused to condemn white supremacy. When asked by moderator Chris Wallace to condemn The Proud Boys, a far-right extremist group, Trump told the group to \"stand back\" and \"stand by\" amid nationwide protests against racism.</p><p>The president has withdrawn from a virtual debate that was due to take place on Thursday, saying he did not want to be muted while speaking.&#160;</p><p>\"I'm not going to waste my time on a virtual debate. That's not what debating is all about,\" he <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/politics/second-trump-biden-debate-will-be-virtual-organizers-say\">told Fox News</a>.</p><p>\"You sit behind a computer and do a debate — it's ridiculous, and then they cut you off whenever they want.\"</p><p>That means the next and final debate between the pair will take place on Thursday, October 22, less than two weeks away from the election on Tuesday, November 3.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://jpmorganchaseco.gcs-web.com/static-files/cfd52059-1fd0-45fd-90d8-60e5c0ff9c89\">third-quarter earnings</a> on Tuesday that beat the consensus estimates of analysts polled by Bloomberg, reflecting a robust jump in trading revenue that stemmed from the pickup in global financial markets from the depths back in March.</p><p>The company, the largest US bank by assets, posted net revenue of $29.9 billion, which was flat in comparison to the same period last year, but still $1.5 billion above estimates.</p><p>&#160;JPMorgan's shares rose 1.7% in pre-market trading.</p><p><strong>Here are the key numbers:</strong></p><ul><li><strong>Net income:</strong> $9.4 billion versus $6.7 billion estimated</li><li><strong>Earnings per share:</strong> $2.92 versus $2.2 estimated</li><li><strong>Revenue:</strong> $29.9 billion versus $28.3 billion estimated</li></ul><p>JPMorgan set aside $611 million as provisions for credit losses, a decrease of $903 million from the previous year, reflecting a comparatively healthier business.</p><p><strong><em>Read More:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-outlook-market-impact-contested-us-elections-deutsche-bank-2020-10\"><em>Deutsche Bank scoured 200 years of US history to uncover how investors should handle a contested election — including 3 past examples and how markets responded</em></a></p><p>\"Home lending benefited from strong production margins, and combined debit and credit card spend showed positive year-over-year growth in September for the first time since the widespread shutdowns,\" chief executive Jamie Dimon said in the earnings release.</p><p>Dimon noted \"significant uncertainty\" felt by the bank during the year worsened by the COVID-19 pandemic, but commended its recovery efforts.&#160;&#160;</p><p>JPMorgan's equity markets division was the most well-performing this quarter, with strong growth across its commodities, credit, and securitized products. Fixed income markets revenue was up 29% to $4.6 billion.</p><p>US equity markets tumbled to their lowest in several years in late March, as widespread lockdowns to stem the spread of coronavirus brought economic activity to a virtual halt.</p><p>But, since then, thanks in large part to the policies put in place by the Federal Reserve to keep borrowing rates low and the flow of credit going into the real economy, major indices, bonds and commodities have rallied sharply.</p><p>Investment banking revenue rose 12% to $2.1 billion driven by higher banking fees that were partially offset by lower advisory fees.</p><p>Net revenue was flat for JPMorgan's commercial banking division, but up 5% in its asset and wealth management arm. Home lending revenue rose 17% to $1.7 billion, driven by higher production margins.&#160;</p><p>JPMorgan's earnings fell&#160;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/jpmorgan-first-quarter-earnings-result-q1-2020-4-1029088969?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest#est#\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">more than 70% in the first quarter</a>, building up credit reserves in response to the pandemic. The bank posted a plunge in net income to $2.9 billion, its lowest level since 2013.</p><p>But in the last six months of the year, the four largest American lenders have more than doubled their reserves for defaulted loans and believe they are now ready to tackle any consumer or business financial pain, according to the <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/what-to-expect-for-bank-earnings-a-bad-quarter-but-not-as-bad-as-before-11602475260?mod=markets_lead_pos2\">Wall Street Journal</a>.&#160;</p><p><strong><em>Read data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">MSCHF</a>&#160;is offering TikTok users thousands of dollars to post videos attacking big businesses it perceives as evil, such as Tesla, Amazon, Facebook, and Palantir.</p><p>MSCHF, an internet group known for&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mschf-company-behind-viral-jesus-shoes-feet-generator-bull-moon-2020-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mschf-company-behind-viral-jesus-shoes-feet-generator-bull-moon-2020-1\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">its cynical, viral products</a>&#160;and whose CEO&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mschf-company-behind-viral-jesus-shoes-feet-generator-bull-moon-2020-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mschf-company-behind-viral-jesus-shoes-feet-generator-bull-moon-2020-1\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">refuses to define what the group actually is</a>, will pay creators up to $20,000 for the \"takedowns\" depending on how many views they get, provided users include one of nine custom sounds the group has created.</p><p>The custom sound for Tesla, for example, inserts Elon Musk's name into Billie Eilish's song \"Bad Guy.\"</p><p>At the lowest level, MSCHF will pay $10 to users attacking TikTok for \"content suppression,\" if the video gets more than 5,000 views.</p><p>TikTok has in the past directed moderators to censor users <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-censorship-users-deemed-ugly-overweight-or-disabled-2020-3\">deemed ugly or overweight</a>. TikTok denies suppressing content or censoring users.</p><p>For its biggest payout, MSCHF will pay $20,000 to users attacking big data firm Palantir for the company's links to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/ice\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"ba3865e126b4945e5c1495dd9dec7d5f\">Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE)</a>. MSCHF will only pay out once at this level — and only if the video gets more than 10 million views.</p><p>The initiative, called&#160;the <a href=\"https://antiadvertisingadvertising.club/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-ga=\"[[\"Embedded Url\",\"External link\",\"https://antiadvertisingadvertising.club/\",{\"metric25\":1}]]g.club/&#34;,{&#34;metric25&#34;:1}]]\">Anti Advertising Advertising Club</a>, launched on Monday. Other companies it wants creators to attack are the NFL, Purdue Pharma, Comcast, and Fashion Nova.</p><p>If any video hits the stated count threshold, users can send the TikTok link to MSCHF, which then will verify the video creator before paying money to a PayPal account.&#160;</p><p>\"If every user's desire is to sell out, we'll happily enable that impulse if it means we can punch at the companies doing the buying,\" <a href=\"https://antiadvertisingadvertising.club/manifesto/\">MSCHF's manifesto</a> reads.</p><p>MSCHF founder and CEO Gabriel Whaley refuses to define the group. \"A brand of what? I don't know. Being a company kills the magic,\" <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mschf-company-behind-viral-jesus-shoes-feet-generator-bull-moon-2020-1\">he told Business Insider</a> in January.&#160;\"We're trying to do stuff that the world can't even define.\"</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-mschf-founder-want-nike-cease-and-desist-fake-collab-2020-7\">MSCHF began selling a shirt in July</a> that features fabric from 10 popular brands including Nike, Supreme, and Adidas. Whaley said the brands did not give MSCHF permission to make the shirts, but that any legal action would help the product grow in value and popularity.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the Al-Arshani)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f85176891aa9e001880b2c5?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn100@2020_1/2020/10/13/12-57-24-142_53eb4180d2da9725.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn4@2020_2/2020/10/13/12-57-29-979_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zvnSfmcaij4:BT03D9L0a88:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn11@2020_4/2020/10/13/12-57-27-228_71977acbbe489ce4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zvnSfmcaij4:BT03D9L0a88:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn36@2020_2/2020/10/13/12-57-30-218_56e2ada0f0a68f48.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn39@2020_3/2020/10/13/12-57-27-289_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zvnSfmcaij4:BT03D9L0a88:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn43@2020_1/2020/10/13/12-57-28-847_49e29d7c028651fc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/zvnSfmcaij4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn72@2020_6/2020/10/13/12-57-26-205_665bf6f7f0aabacc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602593820300},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 20:57:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 20:57:00","title":"A Nevada man was reinfected with the coronavirus — the first confirmed case in the US — and the 2nd time was worse","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/nevada-man-first-confirmed-american-coronavirus-reinfection-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8575ecc255d800190b9822?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus\" height=\"2790\" width=\"5581\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A nurse with a swab for a coronavirus test.\n<p class=\"copyright\">sonreir es gratis/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A Nevada man was infected for a second time with COVID-19 one month after recovering from a first bout, a new study found.</li>\n<li>The case has a \"significant\" impact on how we understand immunity, <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/health-54512034\">one of the authors told the BBC</a>.</li>\n<li>The 25-year-old man &#8212; who had no underlying conditions &#8212; suffered worse symptoms the second time, the study said.</li>\n<li>It is the first such confirmed case in the US and one of only a handful worldwide. Other reinfection cases have been in Belgium, the Netherlands, Hong Kong, and Ecuador.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A Nevada man who had already gone through a bout of COVID-19 was infected a second time with even worse symptoms, doctors say.</p><p>They believe it is the first documented case of reinfection in the US, a rare occurrence that nonetheless suggests having had COVID-19 does not automatically confer immunity.</p><p>The 25-year-old's case was reported in the peer-reviewed journal <a href=\"https://www.thelancet.com/journals/laninf/article/PIIS1473-3099(20)30764-7/fulltext#articleInformation\">The Lancet Infectious Diseases</a>, which outlined how the man, from Washoe County, first got his symptoms on March 25.</p><p>Suffering from a sore throat, a cough, a headache, nausea, and diarrhea, he attended a community testing event on April 18 and was found to be positive for the coronavirus. He had no underlying conditions or immune weaknesses. After he self-isolated for nine days, his symptoms receded and he got well again.</p><p>He took two tests in May, both of which came back negative. But two days after his second negative test, he began to feel unwell again, and a test on June 5 found him to be positive — this time with symptoms that sent him to the hospital. The man has since recovered.</p><h2>Symptoms were worse 2nd time around</h2><p>Differences in the genetic sequencing of the virus indicated that the new infection was not simply the original, dormant infection flaring back up, according to the study.</p><p>The chances of the same strain mutating in a single person in that time are \"remote,\" the report said. It also ruled out the possibility that the man had been infected with both strains but that one had lain dormant until later.</p><p>The Lancet Infectious Diseases report confirms <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/study-researchers-identify-covid-19-reinfection-case-in-nevada-2020-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">early, non-peer-reviewed findings</a> published in an August online preprint.</p><p>During the second infection, the man was found to be short of breath and hypoxic — meaning his blood was short of oxygen. He was sent to the emergency room for oxygen, the report said.</p><p>It's still unclear why the second infection was worse than the first, but the report's authors suggested three possibilities:</p><ol><li>He could have just had a higher dose of the virus on the second infection.</li><li>The second virus could have been a stronger version.</li><li>The immune response from the first infection could have made the second infection worse, <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/health-54512034\">the BBC reported</a>.</li></ol><h2>There's a lot still to know about coronavirus immunity — despite Trump's tweets</h2><p>Discussion of immunity after infection has had even more intense interest than usual since President Donald Trump's doctors announced that he had recovered from the virus, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/white-house-doctor-announces-trump-tested-negative-for-covid-19-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">as Business Insider's John Haltiwanger reported</a>.</p><p>The president has claimed multiple times that he is now \"immune\" — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-labels-trump-tweet-saying-he-has-coronavirus-immunity-as-misleading-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">a claim Twitter flagged as \"misleading.\"</a> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-claims-coronavirus-immunity-but-science-is-unclear-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">As Business Insider's Morgan McFall-Johnsen has reported</a>, the science behind this is far from conclusive.</p><p>The Lancet Infectious Diseases study's findings have \"significant\" implications for how we understand immunity, Dr. Mark Pandori, an associate professor of pathology at the University of Nevada who was a coauthor of the study, <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/health-54512034\">told the BBC</a>.</p><p>\"Our findings signal that a previous infection may not necessarily protect against future infection,\" he said.</p><p>Paul Hunter, a professor of medicine at the University of East Anglia, told the BBC the findings were \"very concerning.\"</p><p>But he pointed out that we would have heard by now if cases like this were common.</p><p>There have been only a handful of confirmed cases of reinfection with the virus — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-reinfection-case-hong-kong-no-cause-for-panic-2020-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">a man from Hong Kong</a> was announced as one such case in August, followed quickly by <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2-new-coronavirus-reinfection-cases-belgium-netherlands-hong-kong-2020-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">two more such cases</a> in Belgium and the Netherlands. An Ecuadorian reinfection has also been confirmed, according to the study.</p><p>\"It is too early to say for certain what the implications of these findings are for any immunization program,\" Hunter told the BBC. \"But these findings reinforce the point that we still do not know enough about the immune response to this infection.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
